en|Mont Blanc massif, aged 23. In the 2010 season of the IFSC Bouldering World Cup,

en|in the overall 2010 standings. Graftiaux was also a multiple lead climbing champion, and had
en|redpointed to 8b (5.13d), and boulder climbed to 7C (V9). Graftiux was a strong alpinist,
en|climbing to mixed grade M11 and ice climbing to grade grade WI6, and the French

en|the Ice Master-Worldcup ice climbing competition in Valle di Daone in Italy.On 21 August 2010,

en|south face of the mountain a boulder came loose. She was not roped up and

en|The Doñana Disaster, also known as the Aznalcollar Disaster or Guadiamar Disaster (Sp: Desastre de
en|Aznalcóllar, Desastre del Guadiamar), was an industrial accident in Andalusia, southern Spain. On 25 April
en|1998, a holding dam burst at the Los Frailes mine, near Aznalcóllar, Seville Province, releasing
en|4–5 million cubic metres of mine tailings. The acidic tailings, which contained dangerous levels of
en|several heavy metals, quickly reached the nearby River Agrio, and then its affluent the River
en|Guadiamar, travelling about 40 kilometres along these waterways before they could be stopped. The Guadiamar
en|is the main water source for the Doñana National Park, a UNESCO World Heritage Site
en|and one of the largest national parks in Europe. The cleanup operation took three years,
en|at an estimated cost of €240 million.The Los Frailes mine is owned by Boliden-Apirsa (formerly
en|Andaluza de Piritas, S.A.), the Spanish subsidiary of Boliden, and produces about 125,000 tonnes of
en|zinc and 2.9 million ounces (about 3,500 metric tonnes) of silver per year.Samuel Guy Endore
en|(July 4, 1901 – February 12, 1970), born Samuel Goldstein and also known as Harry

en|County, Illinois, United States. As of the 2010 census, its population was 10,463 and it
en|contained 4,237 housing units.The township's name commemorates the Battle of Monmouth.The Japanese saw or nokogiri
en|(鋸) is a type of saw used in woodworking and Japanese carpentry that cuts on
en|the pull stroke, unlike most European saws that cut on the push stroke. Japanese saws
en|are the best known pull saws, but they are also used in China, Iran, Iraq,
en|Korea, Nepal and Turkey. Among European saws, both coping saws for woodworking and jeweler's saws
en|for metal working also cut on the pull stroke like Japanese saws. Cutting on the
en|pull stroke is claimed to cut more efficiently and leave a narrower cut width (kerf).
en|On the other hand, a pull stroke does not easily permit putting one's body weight
en|behind a stroke. This can be readily solved by using a vice or clamping. Another
en|disadvantage, due to the arrangement and form of the teeth, is that Japanese saws do
en|not work as well on hardwoods as European saws do. Japanese saws were originally intended
en|for comparatively soft woods like cypress and pine whereas European saws were intended for hard
en|woods like oak and maple. The popularity of Japanese saws in other regions of the
en|world has resulted in the manufacture and production of a number of Japanese saws outside
en|of Japan.Archippus (; Ancient Greek: Ἄρχιππος, "master of the horse") was an early Christian believer
en|mentioned briefly in the New Testament epistles of Philemon and Colossians.Waldenburg is a town in
en|the district Zwickau in Saxony, Germany. The castle was owned by the House of Schönburg
en|from 1378 until 1945. The pottery town of Waldenburg lies in the valley of the
en|Zwickauer Mulde. The environment is characterized by forest areas, river meadows and the hilly landscape
en|of the Erzgebirge foothills. Waldenburg was founded around 1254 and first documented in 1336 as
en|the town of "Waldinberg". The German settlement of the area that later became Waldenburg began
en|with the founding of the monastery in Remse in 1143. The construction of Waldenburg Castle
en|took place between 1165 and 1172. It was built as a security post on the
en|salt trade route at the Mulden crossing. The streets, buildings and remains of the town
en|wall in the upper town still show Walsenburg's roots in the Middle Ages. A look
en|into the multi-story cellar systems of the upper town reveal even more evidence of this.
en|Walsenburg's pottery tradition has been strong for 700 years. Friedrich XI of Schönburg-Waldenburg awarded the
en|Waldenburg potters their first letter of guild in 1388. Salt-glazed Waldenburg stoneware became very famous

en|1987 in Kanagawa) is a Japanese football player. He currently plays for Giravanz Kitakyushu.Edward Dando
en|(c.1803 – 28 August 1832) was a thief who came to public notice in Britain
en|because of his unusual habit of overeating at food stalls and inns, and then revealing
en|that he had no money to pay. Although the fare he consumed was varied, he
en|was particularly fond of oysters, once having eaten 25 dozen (300) of them with a
en|loaf and a half of bread with butter. Dando began his thefts in about 1826
en|and was arrested at least as early as 1828. He would often leave a house
en|of correction and go on an eating spree the same day, being arrested straight away
en|and appearing in court within a few days, only to be put back in prison.
en|On at least one occasion he was placed in solitary confinement after he stole the
en|rations of his fellow prisoners. Most of his activity was in London, although he also
en|spent time in Kent, much of it in the county's prisons. While in Coldbath Fields
en|Prison in August 1832, Dando caught cholera—part of an ongoing pandemic—and died. His death, like
en|his many exploits, was widely and sympathetically reported in both the London daily press and
en|in local newspapers. His name entered into the public argot as a term for someone
en|who eats excessively and does not pay. He was the subject of numerous poems and
en|ballads. In 1837 William Makepeace Thackeray wrote a short story loosely based on Dando; this
en|was also made into a play by Edward Stirling. Charles Dickens wrote about Dando and
en|compared him to Alexander the Great.The 1927 All-Pacific Coast football team consists of American football

en|an open-source documentation generator written in PHP. It automatically parses PHP source code and produces
en|readable API and source code documentation, based on PHPDoc-formatted comments and the structure of the
en|source code itself. It supports documentation of both object-oriented and procedural code. phpDocumentor runs at
en|the command line to create documentation in HTML format. It has support for linking between
en|documentation, incorporating user level documents like tutorials, and creation of highlighted source code with cross
en|referencing to PHP general documentation. phpDocumentor 1.x could parse PHP syntax of PHP 4 up
en|to PHP 5.2.In March 2012, the DocBlox project merged with the 1.x branch of phpDocumentor,
en|resulting in the new major version release of phpDocumentor 2. The first alpha was released

en|7.4.Chung Tai Shan (Chinese: 中台山; pinyin: Zhōng tái shān; Pe̍h-ōe-jī: Tiong-tai-san) is a Taiwan-based international
en|Chan Buddhist monastic order founded by the Ven. Wei Chueh in 1987. The monastery headquarters,
en|Chung Tai Chan Monastery (or Chung Tai Chan Buddhist Temple, 中台禪寺), completed in September 2001,
en|is located in Puli, Nantou County, in central Taiwan. It is the tallest and one
en|of the largest monasteries in both Taiwan and the world, having a height of 136
en|metres (446 ft). Widely admired as an architectural masterpiece because of the mountain monastery's more
en|modern look, the temple is second only to Fo Guang Shan's monastery in physical size
en|and in the number of ordained disciples. The temple follows traditional Chinese Chan teaching, emphasizing
en|sudden enlightenment and gradual cultivation. Richard Seaward Cantrell (1825 – 11 August 1872) was a
en|19th-century Member of Parliament from Dunedin, New Zealand. Cantrell was born in England in 1825.
en|He arrived in Dunedin in 1858 and took over the Commercial Hotel in December of
en|that year.Cantrell was one of four candidates in the 1866 election in the Caversham electorate,
en|coming second but being decisively beaten by Arthur John Burns. Burns resigned after four years
en|but Cantrell did not stand in the resulting 1870 Caversham by-election. The by-election was won
en|by James McIndoe and at the 1871 election, Cantrell defeated McIndoe. On 27 March 1871,
en|Cantrell was one of five candidates for the Otago Provincial Council, also for the Caversham
en|electorate. He comfortably won this election.Cantrell represented the (parliamentary) Caversham electorate until 1872, when he
en|resigned due to ill health. He sent his resignation from Dunedin by mail on 1
en|August and while the resignation was read out by the speaker on 6 August, it
en|took effect on 31 July (i.e. the day prior to sending it; presumably the date
en|shown on the letter). He had also resigned from the provincial council, but as the
en|council was out of session (the 30th session had finished on 31 May), the resignation
en|could not be processed and his representation ended with his death.At the provincial council, three
en|candidates contested the resulting by-election on 15 August: Robert Stout (149 votes), Henry Fish (110
en|votes), and Richard Henry Leary (90 votes), with Stout thus elected. Cantrell's parliamentary resignation caused
en|the 1872 Caversham by-election, which was held on 28 August and won by William Tolmie.

en|not targeted at local Malaysians but rather at upper-middle-class citizens from China who were looking
en|to park their wealth abroad, by offering relatively affordable seafront properties compared to expensive coastal
en|cities within their country such as Shanghai. However, initial strong sales from China collapsed after

en|National Park (Korean: 속리산국립공원, 俗離山國立公園, sometimes spelled "Sokrisan") is located in the center of the
en|Sobaek Mountains range, on the border between the provinces of Chungcheongbuk-do and Gyeongsangbuk-do, South Korea.
en|The area comprises the valleys of Hwayang, Seonyu, and Ssanggok and the 1,058-metre (3,471 ft)
en|mountain Songnisan, which has given the park its name. It was designated as the country's
en|sixth national park in 1970. The park's most popular attraction is one of Korea's largest
en|temples, the Buddhist temple Beopjusa, initially constructed in 653. Songnisan (the Korean letters spell out
en|"Sokrisan" but the name is actually pronounced "Songnisan") became a national park in 1970. It
en|is the sixth-largest of Korea’s mountain parks with an area of 275 km2. The name
en|means “Remote from the Ordinary World”—a reference to its somewhat isolated position in the very
en|center of South Korea. The mountains belong to the southern arm of the greater Sobaek
en|Range, and the park lies on the border between North Chungcheong and North Gyeongsong Provinces.
en|In 1999, someone decided to cash in on the name of a famous set of
en|mountains in Europe by dubbing the ridge that connects Gubyeongsan, Songnisan, Gwaneumbong and Sanhakbong the
en|Chungbuk Alps. The name is a little misleading, as the highest mountain here is only
en|a humble 1,058 meters. On the English brochure available at the tourist center in the
en|Songni-dong Bus Terminal building, it states: “A hiking path was opened and transformed into a
en|commercial product.” This perhaps says something about how Koreans view their mountains and is a
en|hint that hiking here might not always be peaceful and relaxing. The park gets about
en|1.5 million visitors a year. Songnisan is very scenic. On wet days clouds often catch
en|in the valleys between the mountains, creating a dramatic layered effect. In the spring, the
en|area is known for the brilliant pink azaleas that bloom on the mountainsides. The mountains
en|have a craggy look, with many interesting granite outcroppings and cliffs. Songnisan National Park was
en|designated as the sixth national park in Korea in 1970 and was called “Second Geumgang”
en|or “Sogeumgang (Small Geumgang)” because of its spectacular beauty. This rocky mountain is located across
en|many areas in Chungbuk and Gyeongbuk provinces and spans across a total area of 274.541
en|km2. The main peaks Cheonwangbong, Birobong, and Munjangdae are connected along the baekdudaegan mountain ranges
en|(Backbone of Korea) with well developed stone peaks and ridges. Songnisan is connected to other
en|adjacent mountains, and based around Cheonwangbong (1,058 m) in the south, eight peaks are stretched
en|out like a bow including Birobong, Munjangdae, and Gwaneumbong. Songnisan has natural treasures such as
en|the Jeongipumsong (a pine tree that, in Korean legend, was awarded the rank of minister
en|by King Sejo), otter, flying squirrel, and mandarin duck. In addition, there are many bird
en|species that are designated for the purpose of protection by the Ministry of Environment as
en|well as endangered animals such as the small-eared cat and marten. Moreover, a variety of

en|often work in an ambulance alongside another member of staff. Typically, an ambulance will be

en|Telatyn, 40 km (25 mi) east of Tomaszów Lubelski, and 125 km (78 mi) south-east
en|of the regional capital Lublin.In artificial intelligence, eager learning is a learning method in which
en|the system tries to construct a general, input-independent target function during training of the system,
en|as opposed to lazy learning, where generalization beyond the training data is delayed until a
en|query is made to the system. The main advantage gained in employing an eager learning
en|method, such as an artificial neural network, is that the target function will be approximated
en|globally during training, thus requiring much less space than using a lazy learning system. Eager
en|learning systems also deal much better with noise in the training data. Eager learning is
en|an example of offline learning, in which post-training queries to the system have no effect
en|on the system itself, and thus the same query to the system will always produce
en|the same result. The main disadvantage with eager learning is that it is generally unable
en|to provide good local approximations in the target function.Arthur Wontner (21 January 1875 – 10

en|only for the separate protectorate of the Ellice Islands, before extending one year later his
en|mandate to the Gilbert Islands. In 1892, Swayne first arrived in the Ellice Islands, then,
en|from October 1893 to November 1895, he was in the Gilbert Islands with central headquarters

en|lies 99 kilometres (62 miles) south-west of the centre of Brisbane, Australia and is South
en|East Queensland's highest peak at 1,375 metres (4,511 feet). At this elevation, it is the
en|fifth-highest peak in Queensland, after Mount Bartle Frere at 1,622 metres (5,322 feet), Mount Bellenden
en|Ker at 1,593 metres (5,226 feet), Mount Fisher at 1,385 metres (4,544 feet) and Mount
en|Carbine Tableland at 1,383 metres (4,537 feet), all in Far North Queensland. It has an
en|extensive logging history dating back to the mid-19th century. Mount Superbus was originally covered in
en|dense hoop pine forests. Red cedar and other valuable timbers were also heavily logged in
en|the area. It is now part of the Main Range National Park. The peak is
en|a remnant of the Main Range shield volcano which erupted between 25 and 22 million
en|years ago.On the southernmost peak just below the summit lies the wreck of a RAAF
en|Lincoln bomber. It crashed into the mountain in the early hours of Easter Saturday morning
en|on 9 April 1955, during a medical evacuation of a sick baby from Townsville to
en|Eagle Farm airfield in Brisbane. The crew of four RAAF personnel and the two passengers
en|were all killed in this accident. Most of the wreckage still lies near the summit

en|bytecode execution up by up to 20 times, compared to standard Intel CPU with a

en|'pj,' probably first patch was for version 2.9.GNU Binutils is still available as machine definition
en|'pj,' as of Binutil version 2.28. GNU Debugger was once implemented, but code might be
en|lost. Sun Microsystems provided instruction set simulator worked with GDB as SCSL open source code.

en|Spanish painter, primarily of female portraits.A Non-high school district is an American form of public
en|school district which does not itself provide a high school, but instead reimburses nearby public
en|districts with high schools for the education of students in the non-high district. At least
en|two states in the United States — Illinois and Washington — still have districts designated
en|as non-high school districts. Another state, Kentucky, does not use the term, but has four
en|districts that do not operate high schools. Illinois Non-high districts have existed since 1917 and
en|are still provided for by statute. An Illinois non-high district is a special form of
en|high school district consisting of the portion of a county not in any high school
en|district or unit school district. It is separate from any local grade school district. It
en|pays the tuition of eighth grade graduates to nearby high schools, and may provide for
en|their daily transportation. Only one remains: Chester Non-High School District 122, whose territory is in
en|and around Prairie du Rocher in Randolph County. More recent Illinois laws allow a unit
en|school district to deactivate either its elementary schools or its high schools and pay the
en|tuition for their students of the appropriate level to attend nearby districts' schools. There were
en|13 such deactivations between 1984 and 2010. Washington All school districts in the state of
en|Washington are either "high school districts" or "nonhigh school districts". Nonhigh school districts select "serving"
en|high school districts, for which the nonhigh district also contributes to building funds, but any
en|high school with more than a third of the nonhigh district's students is always a
en|"serving" district. Students may attend a serving or non-serving district. Kentucky State law considers all
en|districts to be either "county school districts" or "independent school districts", with the latter defined
en|as a district whose boundaries do not follow a county line, and does not legally
en|distinguish districts by the grades that they choose to teach. However, four districts, all independent,
en|operate only a single K–8 school.Anchorage: A district whose boundaries mostly coincide with those of

en|moon landing in 1969. Like Lunar House, Apollo serves as the headquarters of UK Visas
en|and Immigration, a division of the Home Office in the United Kingdom. The buildings at
en|one time hosted the headquarters of the Property Services Agency (PSA), along with other 1960s
en|office blocks, including those forming part of the Whitgift Centre. The PSA also had offices

en|(Greek: Ρωμαίικο or Ρωμέικο) is a red grape variety indigenous to Greece. Its name derives
en|from the term Romios that is used to refer to modern Greeks (literally Roman as
en|a citizen of the former Byzantine Empire). Romeiko is an indigenous grape found on many
en|Cycladic islands and Crete, prominently in the region of Chania and in particular Kissamos where
en|it thrives. Romeiko vineyards are late maturing and high-yielding, producing high-Baumé must that is mixed
en|with other varieties to give red, rosé and white wines. The pomace is distilled to
en|produce Tsikoudia. Kissamos, a red wine with 13% alcohol content, and Clos de Creta, a
en|white wine, are both made from Romeiko grapes. Romeiko is often used to make the
en|traditional marouvas wine, similar to a sherry.DNA analysis has shown that the similarly named Marvoromaiko
en|is actually an unrelated variety.Mykola Ivanovych Kudritsky (Ukrainian: Микола Іванович Кудрицький, Russian: Николай Иванович Кудрицкий;
en|6 October 1962, in Nikopol – 16 March 1994, in Ra'anana, Israel) was a Ukrainian
en|professional football player. Kudrytsky perished in a car crash while heading back home early in
en|the morning. He was ejected out of his car when it flipped.The Scotch bonnet (Semicassis
en|granulata) is a medium-sized to large species of sea snail, a marine gastropod mollusk in
en|the subfamily Cassinae, the helmet shells and bonnet shells. The common name "Scotch bonnet" alludes
en|to the general outline and color pattern of the shell, which vaguely resemble a tam
en|o' shanter, a traditional Scottish bonnet or cap. The shell is egg-shaped and fairly large,
en|2 to 4 inches (5 to 10 cm) in maximum dimension, with a regular pattern
en|of yellow, orange or brown squarish spots. The surface sculpture of the shell is highly
en|variable: the surface can be smooth and polished, have grooves, be granulated, or even be
en|nodulose on the shoulder of the whorls. This species lives intertidally and subtidally on sandy
en|substrates, and is found primarily in the tropical and subtropical Western Atlantic Ocean, from North
en|Carolina to Uruguay. It is the most common species in this subfamily in North America.
en|A similar-appearing sea snail in the Mediterranean Sea and Northern Atlantic Ocean, Semicassis undulata, is
en|currently considered to be a separate species. The exact taxonomy of Semicassis granulata has been
en|unclear in the past: as well as the current combination, 38 other combinations and synonyms
en|exist. In the spring, the adult females of this species lay eggs in tower-shaped structures.
en|The eggs hatch as veliger larvae, which can float in the plankton for up to
en|14 weeks before settling onto the seabed as tiny snails. Crabs are a predator of
en|this sea snail. After the death of the snails, if the shells are still intact
en|they are often used by hermit crabs. In 1965, in the US, the Scotch bonnet
en|shell was named as a state symbol of North Carolina, the first designation of a
en|US state shell.John Hall was an English professional footballer who played as a winger. James

en|alternatives authorized under Ireland's Personal Insolvency Act 2012; Debt Settlement Arrangements (DSA) and Debt Relief
en|Notices (DRN) are the other two arrangements. A PIA is a legal agreement between a

en|as Middlebury's 12th president in 1963 and served until 1975. Armstrong graduated from Princeton University
en|in 1941 and completed his Ph.D. there in 1949. He served as a professor of
en|classics and Associate Dean without Portfolio at Princeton prior to his arrival at Middlebury.Armstrong led
en|Middlebury through the national political upheaval of the 1960s. On campus, student life for men

en|which allows students to spend four weeks in January to enroll in one intensive course
en|or pursue independent research or internships. Armstrong is credited with laying the groundwork for Middlebury's
en|emergence as a nationally renowned institution, significantly growing the College's enrollment, endowment and physical plant.

en|and later Sørneset in Ålesund, Norway. The airport was, to a varying degree, used between
en|1929 and 1979. It has since been demolished. The first use of Nørvevika was in
en|November 1929 as a temporary base for the Royal Norwegian Navy Air Service. When Norwegian
en|Air Lines commenced scheduled flights along the coast in 1935, they also took the facilities
en|into use. The Navy Air Service returned in 1939 and decided to build a base,
en|but there was no time to carry out the plans before the German invasion the
en|following year. The Luftwaffe used the base for two Arado Ar 196 from 1941 to
en|1943, moving the base to Sørneset during the Second World War. Lufttransport moved to the
en|base in 1946 and carried out commercial flights in 1948 and 1949. After shutting down,

en|English), harbour (British English; see spelling differences), or haven is a sheltered body of water
en|where ships, boats, and barges can be docked. The term harbor is often used interchangeably
en|with port, which is a man-made facility built for loading and unloading vessels and dropping
en|off and picking up passengers. Ports usually include one or more harbors. Alexandria Port in
en|Egypt is an example of a port with two harbors. Harbors may be natural or
en|artificial. An artificial harbor can have deliberately constructed breakwaters, sea walls, or jettys or they
en|can be constructed by dredging, which requires maintenance by further periodic dredging. An example of
en|an artificial harbor is Long Beach Harbor, California, United States, which was an array of
en|salt marshes and tidal flats too shallow for modern merchant ships before it was first
en|dredged in the early 20th century. In contrast, a natural harbor is surrounded on several
en|sides of land. Examples of natural harbors include Sydney Harbour, New South Wales, Australia and

en|kurgan (tumulus) situated in Peredolskaya Volost, near the bank of the Luga River, Batetsky District,
en|Novgorod Oblast, northwestern Russia, about 60 km west of Novgorod. The hill was formerly involved
en|in local liturgical practice. 19th century sources record that three crosses standing on its top,
en|but by the 20th century these had been removed. During the mid 19th century, there
en|used to be processions, with pilgrims walking three times around the hill before ascending it
en|to "listen to the noise" and leave small sacrifices in a pit at the top.
en|People suffering from headache used to put sand from the pit in their ears. These
en|practices are described by A. A. Panchenko in 1998. The site and the associated folk
en|customs were first described by M. Bystrov in 1879. Bystrov records the tradition that the
en|sand from the hill had miraculous power on Trinity Sunday, and that if the hill
en|was ascended on that day, the sound of bells could be heard if one "listened
en|in a special way", and that on this day, pilgrims from as far as 50
en|miles away would come to the hill in hope of curing headaches. The kurgan has
en|not been excavated, but in 2002 a georadar survey was performed by the Russian Federal
en|Geological Institute (ВСЕГЕИ), and in 2003 to 2004, the Institute for the History of Material
en|Culture of the Russian Academy of Sciences has done experimental surveys testing non-intrusive archaeological methods.

en|is 733121.The generalized Lotka–Volterra equations are a set of equations which are more general than
en|either the competitive or predator–prey examples of Lotka–Volterra types. They can be used to model
en|direct competition and trophic relationships between an arbitrary number of species. Their dynamics can be
en|analysed analytically to some extent. This makes them useful as a theoretical tool for modeling
en|food webs. However, they lack features of other ecological models such as predator preference and
en|nonlinear functional responses, and they cannot be used to model mutualism without allowing indefinite population
en|growth. The generalised Lotka-Volterra equations model the dynamics of the populations. This enzyme requires Mg2+.Koubewel

en|Cherenkov Effect Experiment (STACEE), is a gamma ray detector located near Albuquerque, New Mexico. Observations
en|with STACEE began in October 2001 (2001-10) and concluded in June 2007 (2007-06). Gamma rays
en|were observed from objects such as the Crab Nebula, a supernova remnant, and Markarian 421,
en|a blazar. STACEE uses the heliostats and space on the receiver tower of the National
en|Solar Thermal Test Facility (NSTTF) operated by the Sandia National Laboratories on the grounds of
en|the Kirtland Air Force Base. In the daytime, the facility is used for solar energy
en|research. During the night STACEE uses the heliostats to reflect the brief flashes of Čerenkov
en|radiation caused by gamma rays hitting the upper atmosphere to photodetectors mounted in the tower.
en|STACEE is a nonimaging telescope, meaning that it detects the light from a portion of
en|the sky, but does not resolve the light into an image. The detector is operated

en|the music video won Most Popular Music Video.Aviation Maintenance Technician Day is a day of
en|recognition, observed on May 24, that recognizes the efforts of aviation maintenance professionals as well
en|as the achievements of Charles Edward Taylor, the man who built the engine used to
en|power the airplane of the Wright Brothers. The date May 24 was selected to honor
en|the birth date of Taylor. The day of recognition is currently observed by 45 states
en|in the United States. On May 24, 2007, a United States House of Representatives resolution
en|supporting the goals and ideals of a National Aviation Maintenance Technician Day was introduced. Congressman
en|Bob Filner of California was the sponsor of the resolution. On April 30, 2008 the
en|resolution passed by a voice vote[1].Puerto Ricans have both immigrated and migrated to New York
en|City. The first group of Puerto Ricans immigrated to New York City in the mid-19th
en|century when Puerto Rico was a Spanish colony and its people Spanish subjects. The following
en|wave of Puerto Ricans to move to New York City did so after the Spanish–American
en|War in 1898. Puerto Ricans were no longer Spanish subjects and citizens of Spain, they
en|were now Puerto Rican citizens of an American possession and needed passports to travel to
en|the Contiguous United States. That was until 1917, when the United States Congress approved Jones–Shafroth
en|Act which gave Puerto Ricans in Puerto Rico U.S. citizenship with certain limitations. Puerto Ricans
en|living in the mainland United States however, were given full American citizenship and were allowed
en|to seek political office in the states in which they resided. Two months later, when
en|Congress passed the Selective Service Act, conscription was extended to the Puerto Ricans both on
en|the island and on the mainland. It was expected that Puerto Rican men 18 years
en|and older serve in the U.S. military during World War I. The Jones–Shafroth Act also
en|allowed Puerto Ricans to travel between Puerto Rico and the U.S. mainland without the need
en|of a passport, thereby becoming migrants. The advent of air travel was one of the
en|principal factors that led to the largest wave of migration of Puerto Ricans to New
en|York City in the 1950s, known as "The Great Migration". Similar to many other U.S.
en|East Coast cities, Puerto Ricans were the first Hispanic group to move to New York
en|City in large numbers. From 1970 until about 1990, the city's Puerto Rican population was
en|at its height. They represented up to 80% of the city's Hispanic community and 12%
en|of the city's total population. At that time, nearly 70% of Puerto Ricans in the
en|mainland United States lived in New York City. It wasn't until the 1990s that the
en|percentage Puerto Ricans that made up the city's Hispanic community, and the total population as
en|a whole started to decrease, largely due to a declining Puerto Rican population, increasingly diversifying
en|Hispanic community, and New York City's economy rebounding after deindustrialization, which ultimately resulted in a
en|faster growing city population and dwindling Puerto Rican influence. However, since the early 2010s, New
en|York's Puerto Rican population started to grow again, being in the midst of another major
en|migration wave out of Puerto Rico. According to the 2010 census, Puerto Ricans represent 8.9
en|percent of New York City alone (32% of the city's Hispanic community), and 5.5% of
en|New York State as a whole. Of over a million Puerto Ricans in the state,
en|about 70% are present in the city, with the remaining portion scattered in the city's
en|suburbs and other major cities throughout New York State. Although Florida has received some dispersal
en|of the population, there has been a resurgence in Puerto Rican migration to New York
en|and New Jersey, primarily for economic and cultural considerations, topped by another surge of arrivals
en|after Hurricane Maria devastated Puerto Rico in September 2017 – consequently, the New York City
en|Metropolitan Area has witnessed a significant increase in its Nuyorican population, individuals in the region
en|of Puerto Rican descent, from 1,177,430 in 2010 to a Census-estimated 1,494,670 in 2016, maintaining
en|New York's status by a significant margin as the most important cultural and demographic center

en|department.Sahar has been awarded Tamgha-e-Imtiaz by the Government of Pakistan in 2006.The presidential cabinets (German:
en|Präsidialkabinette) were a succession of governments of the Weimar Republic whose legitimacy derived exclusively from
en|presidential emergency decrees. From April 1930 to January 1933, three chancellors, Heinrich Brüning, Franz von
en|Papen, and Kurt von Schleicher were appointed by President Paul von Hindenburg, and governed without
en|the consent of the Reichstag, Germany's lower house of parliament. After Schleicher's tenure, the leader
en|of the Nazis Adolf Hitler succeeded to the chancellorship, ending the Weimar Republic. Article 48
en|of the Weimar Constitution gave the President of Germany (Reichspräsident) the power to pass emergency
en|measures which did not require parliamentary support, as long as the federal cabinet approved of
en|them. After a grand coalition led by chancellor Hermann Müller collapsed, President Paul von Hindenburg
en|appointed the Centre Party politician Heinrich Brüning to the chancellorship. Since Brüning did not command
en|a majority in parliament, he governed exclusively through the president's emergency powers. Whenever the government
en|suffered parliamentary defeats, Hindenburg would dissolve the Reichstag and enable Brüning to stay in office.
en|During Brüning's time in office, Adolf Hitler and his Nazi Party became an influential force
en|in German politics. Brüning legislated to oppose the party's paramilitary activity but was replaced with
en|Franz von Papen, a conservative advisor of the president, who sought to compromise with the
en|forces of the radical right. His short-lived presidential government saw the NSDAP gain the largest
en|share of seats in parliament in the election of July 1932. Unable to overcome parliamentary
en|obstruction, he was succeeded by Kurt von Schleicher, who, in turn, was followed by Hitler
en|on 30 January 1933. The presidential cabinets have been interpreted as a result of the
en|scepticism towards parliamentary government in German society as well as a fundamental shift in political
en|practice towards a strong presidential ruler. Hindenburg's decision to govern without the support of the
en|Reichstag constitutes a milestone on Germany's progression from a multi-party democracy to a totalitarian dictatorship

en|between Penuwch and Bontnewydd in Ceredigion, Wales. It is a Site of Special Scientific Interest
en|partly owned by the Wildlife Trust of South and West Wales. Public access is via
en|a bridlepath from the road. It is a mesotrophic lake located in the headwaters of
en|the River Aeron, whose low nutrient waters are home to a number of locally rare
en|water plants. Waterfowl and passing sea birds can be seen on the lake as can
en|dragonflies, damselflies, and caddis flies in the summer.The lake has a surface area of 5.3
en|hectares (13 acres) and a maximum depth of 8.3 m (27 ft). It lies in
en|a hollow probably scoured out glacially, and is dammed by a moraine. Palynological studies show
en|that it has developed since the last ice age and is a remnant of a
en|larger lake, Llyn Farch, which has otherwise dried up. It is surrounded by pasture grazed
en|by cattle and sheep and at the southern end is a small peat mire. There
en|are tussocks of purple moor-grass and tall cushions of common hair moss and Sphagnum recurvum.
en|In the old peat cuttings, marsh cinquefoil, bog asphodel, bogbean, beaked sedge and Sphagnum species
en|grow. In the open water at the southern end, yellow water lilies and European white
en|water lilies float on the surface, and at the northern end can be found water
en|lobelia, lake quillwort, Littorella uniflora and a few plants of water awlwort, all uncommon species
en|in this area.In the sometimes boggy rough grassland surrounding the lake are also common spike-rush,

en|near Ribchester, Lancashire, England. A Grade II listed structure, located about three quarters of a
en|mile east of the village, it actually crosses the river between the civil parishes of
en|Clayton-le-Dale and Dutton. The bridge carries the two-lane traffic of the B6245 Ribchester Road.Thought to
en|have been constructed in 1774, it is built of sandstone and consists of three segmental
en|arches on triangular cutwaters, with a string course and a solid parapet. The bridge has
en|an overall length 71.8 metres (236 ft) and width of 6.8 metres (22 ft) (deck
en|plus 300-millimetre (12 in)-wide parapets). The central span in the largest at 23.2 metres (76
en|ft) with a rise of 5.5 metres (18 ft), with the others of differing, slightly
en|smaller dimensions.This point on the river is above the tidal limit, the banks approximately 27
en|metres (90 ft) above the Ordnance datum. It has been an important crossing for millennia
en|with the Roman fort here positioned to guard it; however, the origin of the earliest
en|bridge is uncertain. The current bridge's predecessor had been constructed in 1669. William Stukeley in
en|his 'Itinerarium Curiosum', published in 1721, described it as "a noble bridge of four very
en|large arches" half a mile above Ribchester. The county authorities must have been aware of
en|problems, as in 1769 tenders were invited for its reconstruction, but it collapsed during a

en|Green is a residential area in the town of Chadderton in the Metropolitan Borough of
en|Oldham, Greater Manchester. The area is also commonly known as Washbrook.Located in the south east
en|of the town, Butler Green forms a contiguous urban area with Coalshaw Green, Whitegate, Nimble
en|Nook, Block Lane and Hollinwood.Hollinwood Rugby League Club are based at Butler Green on Melrose
en|Fields, the site of the former Melrose Mill.In the United States, a patroon (English: ;
en|from Dutch patroon [paːˈtroːn]) was a landholder with manorial rights to large tracts of land
en|in the 17th century Dutch colony of New Netherland on the east coast of North
en|America. Through the Charter of Freedoms and Exemptions of 1629, the Dutch West India Company
en|first started to grant this title and land to some of its invested members. These
en|inducements to foster colonization and settlement (also known as the "Rights and Exemptions") are the
en|basis for the patroon system. By the end of the eighteenth century, virtually all of
en|the American states had abolished primogeniture and entail; thus patroons and manors evolved into simply
en|large estates subject to division and leases. The deeded tracts were called patroonships and could
en|span 16 miles in length on one side of a major river, or 8 miles
en|if spanning both sides. In 1640, the charter was revised to cut new plot sizes
en|in half, and to allow any Dutch American in good standing to purchase an estate.
en|The title of patroon came with powerful rights and privileges. A patroon could create civil
en|and criminal courts, appoint local officials and hold land in perpetuity. In return, he was
en|required by the Dutch West India Company to – sources vary – establish a settlement
en|of at least 50 families within four years on the land, or "ship fifty colonists
en|to it within four year". As tenants working for the patroon, these first settlers were
en|relieved of the duty of public taxes for ten years, but were required to pay
en|rent to the patroon. A patroonship sometimes had its own village and other infrastructure, including
en|churches. Patroons were entitled to the acquisition of enslaved labor by the Dutch West India
en|Company's Rights and Exemptions Charter. Patroons, often the wealthiest and most influential residents of New
en|Netherland, procured and exploited slaves in almost every part of the colony, although a majority
en|of the slave population remained near New Amsterdam, and farther north, were centered around Fort
en|Orange (Albany, NY) and Rensselaerswijck. Moreover, patroons were essentially the only colonists in New Netherland
en|to own slaves.After the English takeover of New Netherland in 1664 and American independence in
en|1783, the system continued with the granting of large tracts known as manors, and sometimes
en|referred to as patroonships. Ramon B. Neri was a Filipino politician who was the Mayor
en|of Cagayan de Misamis from 1912–1916 and represented Misamis during the 4th Philippine Legislature. Together

en|(Arabic: جامع الأقصى, lit. 'congregational mosque of Al-Aqsa [compound]'), also known as the Qibli Mosque
en|or Qibli Chapel (Arabic: المصلى القبلي, romanized: al-muṣallā al-qiblī, lit. 'prayer hall of the qibla
en|(south)'), is a congregational mosque or prayer hall in the Old City of Jerusalem. In
en|some sources the building is also named al-Masjid al-Aqṣā, but this name and its English
en|translation "Al Aqsa Mosque" itself, is disputed as it can instead apply to the whole
en|compound in which the building sits. The wider compound is also known as the Haram
en|al-Sharif, the Al-Aqsa Mosque compound (or simply Al-Aqsa), and the Temple Mount.During the rule of
en|the Rashidun caliph Umar (r. 634–644) or the Umayyad caliph Mu'awiya I (r. 661–680), a
en|small prayer house on the compound was erected near the mosque's site. The present-day mosque,
en|located on the south wall of the compound, was originally built by the fifth Umayyad
en|caliph Abd al-Malik (r. 685–705) or his successor al-Walid I (r. 705–715) (or both) as
en|a congregational mosque on the same axis as the Dome of the Rock, a commemorative
en|Islamic monument. After being destroyed in an earthquake in 746, the mosque was rebuilt in
en|758 by the Abbasid caliph al-Mansur. It was further expanded upon in 780 by the
en|Abbasid caliph al-Mahdi, after which it consisted of fifteen aisles and a central dome. However,
en|it was again destroyed during the 1033 Jordan Rift Valley earthquake. The mosque was rebuilt
en|by the Fatimid caliph al-Zahir, who reduced it to seven aisles but adorned its interior
en|with an elaborate central archway covered in vegetal mosaics; the current structure preserves the 11th-century
en|outline. During the periodic renovations undertaken, the ruling Islamic dynasties constructed additions to the mosque
en|and its precincts, such as its dome, façade, minarets, and minbar and interior structure. Upon
en|its capture by the Crusaders in 1099, the mosque was used as a palace; it
en|was also the headquarters of the religious order of the Knights Templar. After the area
en|was conquered by Saladin in 1187, the structure's function as a mosque was restored. More
en|renovations, repairs, and expansion projects were undertaken in later centuries by the Ayyubid Sultanate, the
en|Mamluk Sultanate, the Ottoman Empire, the Supreme Muslim Council of British Palestine, and during the
en|Jordanian occupation of the West Bank. Since the beginning of the ongoing Israeli occupation of
en|the West Bank, the mosque has remained under the independent administration of the Jerusalem Islamic
en|Waqf.Al-Aqsa Mosque is located in close proximity to various historical and holy sites in Judaism
en|and Christianity, most notably that of the Temple in Jerusalem. The entire area has consequently
en|held high geopolitical significance, and has been a primary flashpoint in the Israeli–Palestinian conflict.The 1965

en|was taken under the protection of Bishop Dubreil and served for a time as the
en|bishop's secretary.The Belgian Revolution (French: Révolution belge, Dutch: Belgische Revolutie/opstand/omwenteling) was the conflict which led
en|to the secession of the southern provinces (mainly the former Southern Netherlands) from the United
en|Kingdom of the Netherlands and the establishment of an independent Kingdom of Belgium. The people
en|of the south were mainly Flemings and Walloons. Both peoples were traditionally Roman Catholic as
en|contrasted with Protestant-dominated (Dutch Reformed) people of the north. Many outspoken liberals regarded King William
en|I's rule as despotic. There were high levels of unemployment and industrial unrest among the
en|working classes.On 25 August 1830, riots erupted in Brussels and shops were looted. Theatregoers who
en|had just watched the nationalistic opera La muette de Portici joined the mob. Uprisings followed
en|elsewhere in the country. Factories were occupied and machinery destroyed. Order was restored briefly after
en|William committed troops to the Southern Provinces but rioting continued and leadership was taken up
en|by radicals, who started talking of secession.Dutch units saw the mass desertion of recruits from
en|the southern provinces and pulled out. The States-General in Brussels voted in favour of secession
en|and declared independence. In the aftermath, a National Congress was assembled. King William refrained from
en|future military action and appealed to the Great Powers. The resulting 1830 London Conference of
en|major European powers recognized Belgian independence. Following the installation of Leopold I as "King of

en|Bethune-Kennedy House) is a historic residence in Abbeville, Alabama. The house was built around 1870
en|by William Calvin Bethune, a local physician. The house changed hands several times before being
en|acquired by William and Mollie Kennedy in 1885. The Kennedys, who were Henry County farmers,
en|used it as a town house. It remained in the family until 1974, when it
en|was purchased by the local Board of Education. The house was later owned by the
en|Abbeville Chamber of Commerce. The house was built in Creole cottage style, common along the
en|Gulf coast, but more rare inland. The side gable roof has exterior chimneys in each
en|end, and also covers a full-width front porch. A tall frieze is supported by four
en|Doric columns, with matching pilasters on the corners of the house. Twin six-panel entry doors
en|open into separate rooms, each of which contains an original fireplace mantel. The northern room
en|has an enclosed stair hall leading to the finished attic space. The rear originally had
en|a porch and breezeway connected to a kitchen, however this was removed in the early
en|1900s and replaced with an addition containing bedrooms. This addition was removed in the 1970s

en|Perrysburg. Greatest Hits is a compilation album by English reggae group UB40, released in 2008.
en|The album includes all 21 tracks from 11 studio albums and the compilation The Best
en|of UB40: Volume Two.Bray-sur-Somme (French pronunciation: ​[bʁɛ syʁ sɔm], literally Bray on Somme) is a
en|commune in the Somme department in Hauts-de-France in northern France.The 1685 English general election elected
en|the only parliament of James II of England, known as the Loyal Parliament. This was
en|the first time the pejorative words Whig and Tory were used as names for political
en|groupings in the Parliament of England. Party strengths are an approximation, with many MPs' allegiances
en|being unknown. 513 Members of Parliament were returned across 53 counties and 217 boroughs in
en|England and Wales, most returning two members. Only 15 counties and 57 boroughs (a total
en|of 100 seats) had contested elections, with the other candidates being returned unopposed. One borough
en|had a double return, where multiple members were recorded elected, and another was subsequently voided
en|by Parliament, forcing a by-election. While the number of seats had not changed from the
en|previous election, their electorate had been substantially altered by royal influence. Following the Exclusion crisis,
en|ninety-nine boroughs had received new charters, the aim being to eliminate the influence of the
en|Whigs. The Whigs also lost seats in county constituencies - which were not liable to
en|charter manipulation - dropping from around sixty county seats in 1681 to only eight.In the
en|new parliament, the Tories now had their own majority in both houses, Commons and Lords.
en|The exact breakdown of members returned at the election is not clear, but of the
en|525 members who served during the 1685-89 Parliamentary term, including those elected at later by-elections,
en|468 are estimated as Tories and 57 as Whigs. This estimate does not treat any
en|members as uncommitted, and up to 30% of members were recorded as inactive.The election had
en|significant effects on Parliament demographically as well as politically. The newly elected members were mostly
en|inexperienced, with slightly over half never having sat in Parliament before. The majority of these
en|would stand down or lose their seats at the subsequent election in 1689. Members were
en|much more likely to be High Church Anglicans, with very few Presbyterians or Independents compared
en|to other Parliaments of the period. There was an unusually high share of government officials
en|and military officers, and fewer country gentry. Two minors were elected, Peter Legh and the
en|Hon. Thomas Windsor, aged 15 and 16 respectively.The Municipal Building of Texarkana, Arkansas, is located

en|attributes the tale to the Gnostics.The excerpt purports to be the story about the death

en|vision of a man "in the form of an ass" while burning incense in the
en|temple. When he emerges, he is unable to speak at first, but when he is
en|able to relate the vision, those about him kill him. The story is consonant with

en|Howarth Joy (26 September 1880 – 17 February 1966) played first-class cricket for Europeans cricket
en|teams in India and then for Somerset. He was born at Hessle, Yorkshire and died
en|at Winchester, Hampshire. Educated at Winchester College and at New College, Oxford, Joy played as
en|a right-handed tail-end batsman and a left-arm fast-medium bowler in one of the trial matches
en|for the Oxford University cricket team of 1901, but was not selected for a first-class
en|game. From 1906, Joy was employed as a tutor in the household of the Rajah
en|of Dhar in India and then on the staff of the Central India College. In
en|September 1908, he played in three first-class cricket matches for the Europeans team, taking 28
en|wickets in the three matches, including 10 in a match twice. In his first game,
en|against the Parsees in the Bombay Presidency Match in Pune, Joy took seven Parsee wickets
en|for 86 runs in the first innings, and followed that with three for 92 in
en|the second for match figures of 10 for 178: the Parsees still won the match.
en|He was less successful in his second game, against the Parsees again, this time in
en|the Bombay Triangular Tournament, with seven wickets in the match including five for 29 in
en|the first innings, but the Europeans won the match. Finally, in the tournament final, Joy
en|had both his best match and innings bowling performances: seven for 24 followed by four
en|for 50, for a match return of 11 for 74, and the Europeans won the
en|trophy.From 1909, Joy returned to the UK and played a few matches in each of
en|the next four seasons for Somerset, though with limited success. His matches in 1910 and
en|1911 all came late in the season, indicating that he had become a schoolmaster, and
en|only in the last match of 1910, against Yorkshire did he develop anything like his
en|Indian form, finishing with an innings return of five for 44 in a rain-ruined match.
en|There were a further four matches in 1911 without success and in 1912 his sole
en|appearance was against the Australians: he scored 6 and 7 and failed to take a
en|wicket. That was Joy's last first-class cricket match. His obituary in Wisden Cricketers' Almanack in

en|in 2019 at 10,138.Anthocyanins (from Ancient Greek ἄνθος (ánthos) 'flower', and κυάνεος/κυανοῦς (kuáneos/kuanoûs) 'dark blue'),
en|also called anthocyans, are water-soluble vacuolar pigments that, depending on their pH, may appear red,
en|purple, blue, or black. In 1835, the German pharmacist Ludwig Clamor Marquart gave the name
en|Anthokyan to a chemical compound that gives flowers a blue color for the first time
en|in his treatise "Die Farben der Blüthen". Food plants rich in anthocyanins include the blueberry,
en|raspberry, black rice, and black soybean, among many others that are red, blue, purple, or
en|black. Some of the colors of autumn leaves are derived from anthocyanins.Anthocyanins belong to a
en|parent class of molecules called flavonoids synthesized via the phenylpropanoid pathway. They occur in all
en|tissues of higher plants, including leaves, stems, roots, flowers, and fruits. Anthocyanins are derived from
en|anthocyanidins by adding sugars. They are odorless and moderately astringent. Although approved as food and
en|beverage colorant in the European Union, anthocyanins are not approved for use as a food
en|additive because they have not been verified as safe when used as food or supplement
en|ingredients. There is no conclusive evidence that anthocyanins have any effect on human biology or
en|diseases.This article presents a list of Roman provinces in the Late Roman Empire, as found

en|astronomer and physicist Karl Schwarzschild (1873–1916). In 1992, the institute was re-established as Thuringian State
en|Observatory (Thüringer Landessternwarte, TLS). The observatory has the largest telescope located in Germany, which is
en|also the largest Schmidt camera in the world. Made by VEB Zeiss Jena (the branch

en|Creek, Oregon, United States, near the city of Estacada. The farm is part of a
en|640-acre (260 ha) land claim purchased in 1847 by American pioneer Philip Foster. Foster built
en|a store, house, barn, and other structures at the farm. The farmhouse and barn still
en|stand, and replicas of the store, blacksmith shop and log cabin have been built on
en|the site. The Farm is located on the last leg of the Barlow Road, and
en|was an important rest stop for travelers on the Oregon Trail. Exteriors of the Farm
en|are accessible year-round, with interpretive signage. The website at http://philipfosterfarm.com lists visiting hours to see
en|the interiors, with costumed interpreters. The site was listed on the National Register of Historic
en|Places in 1980, and hosts thousands of school children each year for their hands-on Pioneer
en|Life field trips. The Jacknife-Zion-Horseheaven Historical Society3, which owns and operates the site, jokes that
en|Foster Farm is the "First destination resort in the Oregon Territory." Some students at the
en|nearby Summit Learning Charter school come to volunteer and help with tours. They also help
en|with events, and when you arrive at the Farm, are dressed as Pioneers. Coming by
en|is a lovely way to further your child's knowledge of Oregon History. NON PROFIT STATUS3

en|Cider Squeeze Christmas in the CountryAntispila corniella is a moth of the family Heliozelidae. It
en|was described by Kuroko in 1961. It is found in Japan (Kyushu). The wingspan is
en|5–6 mm. The forewings are dark bronzy fuscous with brassy reflections, becoming purplish reflections on
en|the apical half. The basal area is shining leaden-fuscous and the makings are silvery-metallic with
en|yellow or bluish reflections. The hindwings are pale fuscous with feeble purplish lusters. Adult moths
en|usually appear from the end of July to August. Annually, the successive generations replaces the
en|previous generations. The larvae feed on Cornus controversa and Cornus brachypoda. They mine the leaves
en|of their host plant. The mine has the form of a full depth linear-blotch. It
en|is whitish, semitransparent and extends in a line along the leaf margin or in a
en|wavy line. The mine gradually becomes broader. After the third moult, the mine develops into
en|a whitish green blotch. One or two mines may be found in a single leaf.
en|The frass is blackish and is deposited in a line in the linear portion of
en|the mine. In the blotch it appearing like a large black patch in the middle
en|of the mine. Larvae can be found from September to October. Full-grown larvae cut out
en|a case from the end of the mine and descend to the ground. They hibernate
en|within this case. Pupation occurs at the beginning of June of the following year.The Jack

en|ceremony honouring individuals and teams from the world of sports along with sporting achievements throughout
en|the year. It was established in 1999 by Laureus Sport for Good Foundation founding patrons
en|Daimler and Richemont. It is supported by its global partners Mercedes-Benz, IWC Schaffhausen and Mitsubishi
en|UFJ Financial Group. The awards support the work of Laureus Sport for Good, which supports
en|over 160 community projects in more than 40 countries. These programmes aim to use the
en|power of sport to end violence, discrimination and disadvantage, and prove that sport has the
en|power to change the world. The name "Laureus" is derived from the Greek word for
en|laurel, considered a traditional symbol of victory in athletics. The first ceremony was held on
en|25 May 2000 in Monte Carlo, at which South African president Nelson Mandela gave the
en|keynote speech. As of 2020, awards are made annually in eight categories, with a number
en|of discretionary categories irregularly recognised. The recipient of each award is presented with a Laureus
en|statuette, created by Cartier, at an annual ceremony held in various locations around the world.
en|As of 2020, the ceremonies have been held in eleven different cities, and are broadcast
en|in at least 160 countries. Swiss tennis player Roger Federer holds the record for the
en|most awards with six, five for Sportsman of the Year and one for Comeback of
en|the Year. Serena Williams holds the record for most awards held by a female with
en|five, four for Sportswoman of the Year and one for Comeback of the Year. A
en|number of awards have been rescinded, namely those presented to American cyclist Lance Armstrong, American
en|sprinter Marion Jones and Canadian amputee sprinter Earle Connor, each of whom were subsequently found

en|a martial art but has expanded into other domains of practice such as health or

en|a greater extent.In the theory of radiative transfer, of either thermal or neutron radiation, a
en|position and direction-dependent intensity function is usually sought for the description of the radiation field.
en|The intensity field can in principle be solved from the integrodifferential radiative transfer equation (RTE),
en|but an exact solution is usually impossible and even in the case of geometrically simple
en|systems can contain unusual special functions such as the Chandrasekhar's H-function and Chandrasekhar's X- and
en|Y-functions. The method of discrete ordinates, or the Sn method, is one way to approximately

en|Steuart collection.In the mathematical area of topology, a train track is a family of curves
en|embedded on a surface, meeting the following conditions: The curves meet at a finite set
en|of vertices called switches. Away from the switches, the curves are smooth and do not
en|touch each other. At each switch, three curves meet with the same tangent line, with
en|two curves entering from one direction and one from the other.The main application of train
en|tracks in mathematics is to study laminations of surfaces, that is, partitions of closed subsets
en|of surfaces into unions of smooth curves. Train tracks have also been used in graph

nl|De soort komt voor in Brazilië.Boulevard Voltaire is een straat in het 11e arrondissement van
nl|de Franse hoofdstad Parijs.De boulevard begint op Place de la République en eindig bij Place
nl|de la Nation. Voorheen heette deze straat boulevard du Prince Eugène. Op nummer 50 staat

nl|het gemeentehuis van het 11e arrondissement.Aangeleerde hulpeloosheid (Engels: learned helplessness of learnt helplessness) is het
nl|verschijnsel waarbij een mens of dier geleerd heeft dat hij geen invloed kan uitoefenen op
nl|de gebeurtenissen die hem overkomen. Martin Seligman publiceerde in 1967 de resultaten van een dierproef
nl|die in duidelijke tegenspraak waren met de toen heersende opvatting uit het behaviorisme van Burrhus
nl|Skinner. In dit zogenaamde "yoked control"-experiment ondergaan twee dieren meermaals elektrische schokken. Het eerste dier
nl|heeft de mogelijkheid de duur van de schok te bekorten, door bijvoorbeeld op een knop
nl|te drukken. Voor beide dieren stopt dan de schok. Het dier dat de schok niet
nl|kan beïnvloeden heeft na verloop van tijd een aanmerkelijk slechtere gezondheid. Het is ook niet
nl|meer in staat te leren. In een vervolgexperiment werden beide dieren in een zogenaamde "shuttle-box"
nl|gezet: een kooi die door een lage afscheiding in tweeën gedeeld is. In de ene
nl|helft ondergaan beide dieren regelmatig een schok, maar door over de afscheiding te springen, kunnen
nl|ze de schok vermijden. Het dier dat in het eerste experiment de controle had, leert
nl|dit, zoals door het behaviorisme voorspeld, snel. Het tweede dier leert dit echter niet: het
nl|lijdt weliswaar onder de schok, maar onderneemt niets om deze te vermijden: het heeft geleerd
nl|passief en hulpeloos te zijn. Volgens Seligman zou bij mensen aangeleerde hulpeloosheid het mechanisme kunnen
nl|zijn dat op den duur leidt tot psychische stoornissen zoals depressie. Meer algemeen treedt aangeleerde
nl|hulpeloosheid op wanneer mensen of dieren geen adequate terugkoppeling krijgen over hun eigen handelen. Ze
nl|kunnen zo niet leren welke handelingen effectief zijn in het bereiken van een bepaald doel,
nl|waardoor ze zich uiteindelijk hulpeloos en passief zullen opstellen. Finkelstein en Ramey (1977) vonden dit
nl|verschijnsel ook bij baby's. De eerste baby kon een mobile boven de wieg laten bewegen
nl|door zijn hoofd te bewegen, de tweede kon alleen naar het bewegende mobile kijken. Als
nl|de tweede baby de beweging van het mobile kon aansturen, ontdekte hij niet meer dat
nl|hij invloed kon uitoefenen op het mobile. In de dagelijkse praktijk is het concept van
nl|"aangeleerde hulpeloosheid" belangrijk bij de opvoeding van kinderen, maar ook in ziekenhuizen, verpleeghuizen, gevangenissen, in
nl|rampsituaties als hongersnood en oorlog en in concentratiekampen. Niet ieder mens reageert op hulpeloosheid met
nl|passiviteit en depressie. Dit is mede afhankelijk van de attributie, dat wil zeggen waar iemand
nl|de oorzaak van zijn lijden zoekt: in zichzelf of buiten zichzelf. Julie Greciet (Bayonne, 27
nl|november 1986) is een Franse golfprofessional. Ze debuteerde in 2009 op de Ladies European Tour.NGC

nl|Aan het begin van zijn heerschappij versloeg hij de Bourgondiërs en begon een vestigingspolitiek in
nl|het Berner Oberland en het gebied rond het Vierwoudstrekenmeer. Zo breidde hij de stad Thun
nl|verder uit en stichtte hij de stad Bern, die hij tot het middelpunt van zijn
nl|heerschappij uitbouwde. Bij de Slag bij Ulrichen slaagde hij er niet in zijn heerschappij uit
nl|te breiden tot het kanton Wallis. In 1198 werd Berthold V door een minderheid tot
nl|opvolger van keizer Hendrik IV van het Heilige Roomse Rijk verkozen. Door af te zien
nl|van de keizerskroon ten gunste van Filips van Zwaben, consolideerden de Zähringers hun bezittingen in
nl|de Ortenau, Breisgau en het huidige Zwitserland door de rechten te bemachtigen over het Allerheiligenklooster,
nl|Schaffhausen en Breisach. In 1200 begon Berthold V de bouw van het Munster van Freiburg.

nl|in 1904 door Topsent.In de muziektheorie is een toonklasse (Engels: pitch-class) een verzameling (het totaal)
nl|van tonen die onderling een veelvoud van een octaaf verschillen. Door de toonklassen te beschouwen
nl|worden als het ware alle tonen teruggebracht tot binnen één octaaf. De toonklasse die de
nl|stamtoon C bevat, kortweg de toonklasse van C genoemd, is dus {..., C−2, C−1, C0,
nl|C1, C2, C3 ...}Soms gaat men nog verder door alle tonen die bij het klinken
nl|een veelvoud van een octaaf verschillen tot dezelfde toonklasse te rekenen. In de gelijkzwevende stemming
nl|bevat de toonklasse van C dan ook de tonen Bis en Deses doorheen alle octaven.
nl|Het gehele toonmateriaal is dan gereduceerd tot 12 toonklassen. Deze 12 toonklassen worden wel genummerd

nl|1892 – Raivola (Karelië), 24 juni 1923) was een Fins-Zweedse dichteres. Södergran werd op 4
nl|april 1892 geboren in Sint-Petersburg als dochter van Matts en Helena Södergran. Toen Edith enkele
nl|jaren oud was kocht de familie een zomerhuis in de stad Raivola, waar Edith vele
nl|zomers zou doorbrengen. Vanaf 10-jarige leeftijd ging ze naar school aan de Petrischule te Sint-Petersburg,
nl|waar ze tot 1909 zou blijven. Twee jaar daarvoor, in 1907, overleed haar vader aan
nl|tuberculose en in het jaar daarop werd ook bij haar deze ziekte geconstateerd. Ze werd
nl|naar een sanatorium gestuurd, maar daar voelde zij zich niet thuis. Gevoelens van gevangenschap, veroorzaakt
nl|door de ziekte en het sanatorium, zijn terugkerende thema's in haar poëzie. In oktober 1911
nl|reisden Edith en haar moeder naar Arose, te Zwitserland, alwaar zij door verscheidene artsen werd
nl|onderzocht. Na een aantal maanden werd zij naar het Davos-Dorf sanatorium overgeplaatst. In mei 1912
nl|was haar conditie voldoende verbeterd en kon zij weer huiswaarts keren. De ziekte keerde later
nl|echter terug, waardoor zij in 1923 kwam te overlijden in haar huis te Raivola. Ze
nl|werd slechts 31 jaar oud. Haar huis werd verwoest tijdens de Tweede Wereldoorlog. Tijdens haar
nl|leven kreeg ze weinig erkenning, maar vandaag de dag wordt zij beschouwd als een van
nl|meest vooraanstaande dichters van Finland en een van de belangwekkendste modernistische dichters van Scandinavië. Zij
nl|was de eerste Fins-Zweedse modernist en was beïnvloed door het Franse symbolisme, het Duitse expressionisme
nl|en het Russische futurisme. Haar gedichten worden gekarakteriseerd door een vrij ritme en een zachtaardige
nl|intimiteit, waardoor ze goed toegankelijk zijn voor de lezer. Haar eerste werk, Gedichten, bevat een
nl|aantal van haar bekendste liefdesgedichten, die geïnspireerd werden door een mislukte liefdesaffaire. In haar latere
nl|werk schiep Södergran sterke, profetische beelden die haar critici schokten. Haar laatste werk, Het land
nl|dat niet is, is een collectie van teruggetrokken, intieme gedichten die zij schreef kort voor
nl|haar overlijden. Zij werden verzameld door de auteur Hagar Olsson en postuum gepubliceerd.Tomás Garrido Canabal
nl|(Playas de Catazajá, 20 september 1891 - Los Angeles, 8 april 1943) was een Mexicaanse
nl|politicus, caudillo, en gouverneur van de deelstaat Tabasco, die bekendstond om zijn gewelddadige antiklerikale politiek.
nl|Garrido Canabal werd geboren in de haciënda Catazajá in het uiterste noorden van Chiapas. Hij
nl|studeerde rechten in Campeche en raakte tijdens de Mexicaanse Revolutie betrokken in de lokale politiek.
nl|Vanaf 1915 vervulde hij een aantal juridische en politieke functies in de Mexicaanse deelstaat Tabasco.
nl|In 1920 stelde hij zich kandidaat voor het gouverneurschap van die staat. In die verkiezing
nl|nam hij het op tegen een neef met wie hij al jaren ruzie had. Garrido
nl|wist de verkiezing te winnen. Tijdens zijn gouverneurschap toonde hij zich een actief voorstander van
nl|antiklerikale wetgeving. Zo verplichtte hij alle priesters in Tabasco te trouwen, terwijl katholieke priesters gehouden
nl|zijn aan het celibaat. Verder verordende hij dat er nog maar één priester per honderdduizend
nl|inwoners mocht zijn. Hij plunderde kerken of liet ze sluiten, verwijderde religieuze afbeeldingen waaronder kruizen
nl|op grafstenen. Op zijn boerderij noemde hij een stier God, een ezel Jezus, een koe
nl|Maagd van Guadalupe en een os paus. Zijn kinderen noemde hij Lenin en Lucifer en
nl|op zijn visitekaartjes noemde hij zichzelf 'de persoonlijke vijand van God'. Hij stond erop dat
nl|zijn ondergeschikten hem groetten met "God bestaat niet", waarop hij steevast antwoordde "en dat heeft
nl|hij nooit gedaan". Ook vaardigde hij een verbod uit op alcohol, dat hij als vijand
nl|gelijkstelde aan religie. Zijn eerste termijn eindigde in 1924, toen hij verdreven werd door de
nl|aanhangers van Adolfo de la Huerta, die in opstand was gekomen tegen president Álvaro Obregón.
nl|Dat jaar werd Obregón opgevolgd door de radicale Plutarco Elías Calles, waarvan Garrido een groot
nl|aanhanger was. Hij steunde Calles' antiklerikale wetgeving en diens strijd tegen de cristero's, de katholieke
nl|rebellen die in opstand waren gekomen. Door de grondwetswijziging die herverkiezing mogelijk maakte, bedoeld om
nl|Obregón in 1928 weer tot president gekozen te laten worden, wist hij in 1931 voor
nl|een tweede keer tot gouverneur gekozen te worden. Dat jaar richtte hij de 'roodhemden' op,
nl|een paramilitaire organisatie die katholieken terroriseerde. Ook richtte hij de Radicale Socialistische Partij van Tabasco
nl|(PRST) op. Hij wilde met al zijn antiklerikale activiteiten een atheïstische en rationele 'nieuwe mens'
nl|creëren. Dit probeerde hij ook te bereiken door kinderen op school een 'rationalistische' opvoeding mee
nl|te geven. Hoewel zijn extreme antiklerikalisme niet erg populair was werd hij toch gewaardeerd wegens
nl|de stimulans die hij gaf aan de economie van Tabasco. Hij maakte van Tabasco een
nl|belangrijke exporteur van bananen; Tabasco kon onder zijn regering wedijveren met Honduras, de 'bananenrepubliek' bij
nl|uitstek. In 1934 werd in Tabasco, als een van de eerste staten in Mexico, het
nl|vrouwenkiesrecht ingevoerd. In 1934 werd Garrido benoemd tot minister van landbouw. Nadat Calles echter een
nl|jaar later uit de gratie was gevallen bij president Lázaro Cárdenas ontsloeg deze Garrido van
nl|zijn ambt en zette hem het land uit. Garrido vluchtte naar Costa Rica. Kort daarna
nl|werden de roodhemden ontbonden. Op latere leeftijd kon Garrido weer terugkeren naar Mexico. De meningen
nl|over Tomás Garrido Canabal zijn sterk verdeeld. Volgens sommigen was hij een vooruitstrevend heerser die
nl|Tabasco zowel in sociaal als economisch opzicht de moderne tijd inleidde. Anderen noemen hem een
nl|machtswellustige dictator en vergelijken hem met de totalitaire leiders uit de jaren 30. De luitenant
nl|uit Graham Greene's roman The Power and the Glory is gebaseerd op Garrido Canabal. Deze
nl|luitenant is de tegenstander van een "whiskeypriester", een motief dat ook vaak voorkwam in Garrido's
nl|anti-katholieke propaganda.Corematura is een geslacht van vlinders van de familie spinneruilen (Erebidae), uit de onderfamilie
nl|Arctiinae.Borotín (Duits: Borotin) is een Tsjechische gemeente in de regio Zuid-Moravië, en maakt deel uit

nl|Harrison Gray Dyar Jr.. De soort komt voor in Panama.De World Medical Association of WMA
nl|is een internationale vereniging die artsen vertegenwoordigt. De vereniging werd gesticht op 17 september 1947.
nl|Dokters van 27 verschillende landen kwamen samen op de eerste algemene vergadering van de WMA
nl|in Parijs. De organisatie werd gesticht om de onafhankelijkheid van artsen te verzekeren en om
nl|altijd de beste verzorging te verzekeren. Dit was vooral belangrijk voor dokters na de Tweede
nl|Wereldoorlog. Daarom is de WMA altijd een onafhankelijke confederatie van vrije professionele verenigingen geweest. De
nl|vereniging wordt gefinancierd door jaarlijkse bijdragen van haar leden, tachtig nationale medische verenigingen. De WMA
nl|voorziet in een forum voor haar leden om vrij te kunnen communiceren, actief te kunnen
nl|meewerken en een overeenkomst te bereiken over de hoge standaarden van de medische ethiek en
nl|de professionele bekwaamheid. De organisatie wil ook de professionele vrijheid van artsen over de hele
nl|wereld promoten. Deze unieke samenwerking vergemakkelijkt de verzorging van patiënten in een gezonde omgeving en
nl|verbetert de levenskwaliteit voor iedereen. De WMA houdt zich vooral bezig met de ethische onderdelen
nl|van het medische beroep en behandelt internationale codes op gebieden als de medische ethiek, de
nl|patiëntenrechten, onderzoek over de menselijke thema’s, ziekenzorg, militaire slachtoffers of martelen van gevangenen en gebruik
nl|en misbruik van drugs. De WMA is officieel verbonden met de Wereldgezondheidsorganisatie. Ze werkt ook
nl|samen met vele andere organisaties op medisch terrein, in het bijzonder de World Health Professions
nl|Alliance, een verbond van professionele verenigingen voor artsen, verpleegkundigen en apothekers. Het belangrijkste orgaan van
nl|de WMA is de algemene vergadering die jaarlijks samenkomt en de belangrijkste beslissingen neemt. De
nl|vergadering bestaat uit verschillende afgevaardigden van de nationale organisaties, de officiers en leden van de
nl|raad van de WMA en vertegenwoordigers van de vennootschappen. De vergadering verkiest de WMA-raad iedere
nl|twee jaar met vertegenwoordigers uit elk van de zes WMA-regio’s, namelijk Afrika, Azië, Europa, Latijns-Amerika,
nl|Noord-Amerika en Oceanië. De voorzitter van de raad, die om de twee jaar door de
nl|WMA-raad wordt verkozen is het politieke hoofd van de organisatie. De woordvoerder van de WMA
nl|is de president die jaarlijks wordt verkozen op de vergadering. Als hoofd van de uitvoerende
nl|macht van de WMA werkt de secretaris-generaal voltijds op het secretariaat.Cardiodectes asper is een eenoogkreeftjessoort

nl|de Noord-Franse stad Rijsel werd geopend in 1983. De besturing van de metrovoertuigen vindt volledig
nl|automatisch plaats, zonder bestuurders, via het Franse VAL-system (Véhicule Automatique Léger = licht automatisch voertuig).
nl|De treinen zijn slechts 2,2 meter breed en 26 meter lang, en bestaan uit twee
nl|gekoppelde rijtuigen. De treinen rijden op luchtbanden en gebruiken alleen bij calamiteiten en op het
nl|remiseterrein stalen hulpwielen. Er zijn 60 metrostations, die reiken tot aan de Belgische grens. Elk
nl|station heeft perrons van 52 meter lang en er kunnen dus twee metrostellen aan elkaar
nl|gekoppeld worden bij drukte. Bij alle perrons is de toegang tot de sporen afgesloten door
nl|schuifdeuren die enkel geopend zijn wanneer er zich een metrostel in het station bevindt. Elk
nl|treinstel heeft een capaciteit van 156 personen. De bouw van de eerste lijn startte in
nl|1978. Het eerste deel van het metronet werd officieel geopend op 25 april 1983 tussen
nl|de stations 4 Cantons en République. Op 2 mei 1984 werd lijn 1 in zijn
nl|totaal opgeleverd (13,5 km lang). Lijn 2 werd geopend op 3 april 1989. De lijn
nl|is 32 km lang en heeft 43 stations. De voertuigen van de metro van Rijsel
nl|zijn van het VAL-systeem. Transpole, het vervoerbedrijf van Rijsel, heeft 83 metrovoertuigen type Val 206
nl|en 60 van het type Val 208. De treinen hebben een maximumsnelheid van 80 km/h.

nl|maart 2003) was een diplomaat en heraldicus in dienst van de Heilige Stoel. Door zijn
nl|publicaties en zijn samenwerking met paus Johannes XXIII en paus Johannes Paulus I was Heim
nl|een zeer invloedrijk heraldicus en hervormde hij de heraldiek van de Katholieke Kerk. Bruno Bernard
nl|Heim was in 1963 door Johannes XXIII tot titulair aartsbisschop van Xanto "in partibus infidelium"
nl|benoemd. Heim vervolgde zijn diplomatieke loopbaan. De charmante diplomaat werd na diplomatieke posten in Finland,
nl|Duitsland, Oostenrijk en Egypte belast met een moeilijke taak: het aanknopen van diplomatieke relaties tussen
nl|het Verenigd Koninkrijk en de Heilige Stoel. Daarin is hij geslaagd en Heim werd de
nl|eerste pauselijke nuntius aan het "Hof van Sint-James" (pauselijk ambassadeur in Londen). De in het
nl|Zwitserse Olten geboren Heim illustreerde op zijn zestiende voor het eerst een boek over heraldiek.
nl|Ook tijdens zijn studies, Heim promoveerde na gestudeerd te hebben in Freiburg en Solothurn tot
nl|doctor in de Philosophie aan het "Angelicum", de Pontificia Università San Tommaso Aquino in Rome,
nl|bleef die belangstelling bestaan. In 1946 promoveerde hij een tweede maal, ditmaal tot doctor in
nl|het canonieke recht aan de Romeinse Pontificia Università Gregoriana. In 1938 werd Heim tot priester
nl|gewijd en daarna werkte hij 4 jaar als kapelaan in Zwitserland. Hij volgde in 1942
nl|een opleiding tot diplomaat in Rome en werd in 1944 belast met de zielszorg voor
nl|Italiaanse en Poolse vluchtelingen en geïnterneerde militairen in het neutrale Zwitserland. In 1947 werd Heim
nl|op de Parijse nuntiatuur secretaris van aartsbisschop Angelo Roncalli, de latere Paus Johannes XXIII. Beiden
nl|waren in kerkelijke heraldiek geïnteresseerd en waren "verontwaardigd over de onkunde, het misbruik en de
nl|slechte smaak" die alom te zien waren. Hun vruchtbare samenwerking leidde tot wat een "renaissance
nl|van de kerkelijke heraldiek" wordt genoemd. Uiteraard ontwierp Heim het wapen van de eerder tot
nl|patriarch van Venetië benoemde en op 18 oktober 1958 tot paus gekozen Roncalli. Mgr. Heim
nl|was ook verantwoordelijk voor de ontwerpen van de wapens van de pausen Paulus VI, Johannes
nl|Paulus I en Johannes Paulus II. Heim was, door tijdsdruk, niet betrokken geweest bij het
nl|ontwerp van het wapen van Roncalli als patriarch van Venetië. De patriarch ontwierp zijn eigen
nl|wapen en maakte zijn excuus en bij de vaststelling van het pauselijk wapen revancheerde de
nl|paus zich. Het was Johannes' bedoeling geweest om Bruno Bernard Heim als heraldische autoriteit in
nl|het Vaticaan te benoemen. Heim zou dan wereldwijd de kerkelijke heraldiek hebben kunnen hervormen. Heim
nl|heeft deze positie afgeslagen, omdat heraldiek in zijn opvatting een kwestie van goede smaak en
nl|kunstzinnigheid is en een goed voorbeeld en overredingskracht meer bewerken dan dwang en reglementeringen. Strenge
nl|regels zouden de expressie in de heraldiek ook kluisteren. De methode die Heim en de
nl|paus kozen was het adviseren van de nuntiï in diverse landen in de hoop dat
nl|het voorbeeld van een fraai en heraldisch correct wapen van de nuntius de geestelijken de
nl|juiste weg zou wijzen en zou inspireren. Een methode die goed paste bij de stijl
nl|van de charmante maar even overtuigende als vasthoudende diplomaat. Roncalli heeft een groot succes gehad;
nl|gezaghebbende schrijvers als Peter Bander van Duren spreken van een "renaissance van de kerkelijke heraldiek".
nl|Na andere posten bekleed te hebben besloot Heim zijn carrière als "Apostolisch Pro-Nuntius" in Londen.
nl|De heraldiek van de rooms-katholieke geestelijken in Engeland en Schotland is een juridisch probleem, omdat
nl|niemand in deze landen een wapen mag voeren zonder toestemming van de vier wapenkoningen. Kerkelijke
nl|wetgeving en nationale wetgeving kunnen daar botsen en Engeland en Schotland, staten met een staatskerk,
nl|staan de katholieke bisdommen en instellingen geen wapens toe. Prelaten en priesters kunnen wel persoonlijke
nl|wapens ter goedkeuring voorleggen. Heim slaagde erin om diplomatieke banden tussen het Vaticaan en het
nl|Verenigd koninkrijk te regelen, maar de veel moeilijker kwestie van het wapenrecht bleef onopgelost. Heim

nl|jongens en meisjes moeten zijn. Het geslacht van de leraar was belangrijk, voor de meisjes
